				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Corp.">Microsoft Corp.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Microsoft Corporation</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology company</a> with headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Redmond,_Washington" title="Redmond, Washington">Redmond, Washington</a>. It develops, manufactures, licenses, supports, and sells <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">computer software</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computers</a>, and related services. Its best known software products are the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> line of <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office</a> <a href="/wiki/Productivity_software#Office_suite" title="Productivity software">suite</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Explorer" title="Internet Explorer">Internet Explorer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Edge</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a>. Its flagship hardware products are the <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">Xbox</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">video game consoles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Surface" title="Microsoft Surface">Microsoft Surface</a> lineup of <a href="/wiki/Touchscreen" title="Touchscreen">touchscreen</a> personal computers. In 2016, it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_software_companies" title="List of the largest software companies">world's largest software maker</a> by revenue (currently <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet</a>/<a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> has more revenue).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The word "Microsoft" is a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of "microcomputer" and "software".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Microsoft is ranked No. 30 in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Microsoft href="#cite_note-FY19-Q4-1">[1]</a></sup> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Net_income" title="Net income">Net income</a></div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$39.2 billion</span><sup id="cite_ref-FY19-Q4_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY19-Q4-1">[1]</a></sup> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Asset" title="Asset">Total assets</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$286.55 billion</span><sup id="cite_ref-FY19-Q4_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY19-Q4-1">[1]</a></sup> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$102.33 billion</span><sup id="cite_ref-FY19-Q4_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY19-Q4-1">[1]</a></sup> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> 151,163<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.microsoft.com">www<wbr></wbr>.microsoft<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Microsoft was founded by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen" title="Paul Allen">Paul Allen</a> on April 4, 1975, to develop and sell <a href="/wiki/BASIC" title="BASIC">BASIC</a> <a href="/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)" title="Interpreter (computing)">interpreters</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Altair_8800" title="Altair 8800">Altair 8800</a>. It rose to dominate the personal computer operating system market with <a href="/wiki/MS-DOS" title="MS-DOS">MS-DOS</a> in the mid-1980s, followed by Microsoft Windows. The company's 1986 <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO), and subsequent rise in its share price, created three billionaires and an estimated 12,000 millionaires among Microsoft employees. Since the 1990s, it has increasingly diversified from the operating system market and has made a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Microsoft" title="List of mergers and acquisitions by Microsoft">corporate acquisitions</a>, their largest being the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/LinkedIn" title="LinkedIn">LinkedIn</a> for $26.2 billion in December 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> followed by their acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Skype_Technologies" title="Skype Technologies">Skype Technologies</a> for $8.5 billion in May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Microsoft&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Microsoft is market-dominant in the <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC_compatible" title="IBM PC compatible">IBM PC compatible</a> operating system market and the office software suite market, although it has lost the majority of the overall operating system market to <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The company also produces a wide range of other consumer and enterprise software for desktops, laptops, tabs, gadgets, and servers, including <a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" title="Web search engine">Internet search</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Bing_(search_engine)" title="Bing (search engine)">Bing</a>), the digital services market (through <a href="/wiki/MSN" title="MSN">MSN</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mixed_reality" title="Mixed reality">mixed reality</a> (<a href="/wiki/Microsoft_HoloLens" title="Microsoft HoloLens">HoloLens</a>), cloud computing (<a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Azure" title="Microsoft Azure">Azure</a>), and software development (<a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Visual_Studio" title="Microsoft Visual Studio">Visual Studio</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Steve_Ballmer" title="Steve Ballmer">Steve Ballmer</a> replaced Gates as CEO in 2000, and later envisioned a "devices and services" strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> This unfolded with Microsoft acquiring <a href="/wiki/Danger_Inc." title="Danger Inc.">Danger Inc.</a> in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> entering the personal computer production market for the first time in June 2012 with the launch of the Microsoft Surface line of <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>, and later forming <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Mobile" title="Microsoft Mobile">Microsoft Mobile</a> through the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a>'s devices and services division. Since <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a> took over as CEO in 2014, the company has scaled back on hardware and has instead focused on <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a>, a move that helped the company's <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">shares</a> reach its highest value since December 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>Earlier dethroned by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> in 2010, in 2018 Microsoft reclaimed its position as the most valuable publicly traded company in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In April 2019, Microsoft reached the <span class="nowrap">trillion-dollar</span> <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market cap</a>, becoming the third U.S. public company to be valued at over $1 trillion after Apple and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
